The Economic Value of "Economic Wife" 261

— But Ling

Considering the standards by which most people choose a wife, the most important are nothing more than these few points:

(1) "Youth," with youth to the level of "sweet sixteen" and "budding years" being the most satisfying degree;

(2) "Beauty," with the beauty of a goddess, "flower-like countenance," and "delightful appearance" being the highest ideal; in addition, such things as "gentle disposition," "sound physique," and similar social standing are also some of the important conditions. As for whether this wife can help her husband in production, or whether she can be economically self-reliant, this point is generally not given much attention.

Having a "wife" at home who only knows how to consume and does not engage in production is, of course, not a problem for wealthy men. Not to mention one, even having three wives and four concubines is like buying a few more toys, a few mannequin-like foreign dolls; there is never no place to put them. In the event that the wives and concubines become "uneasy in their positions" and "fight" each other, there is also a method of "dismissal." As long as good luck shines, all the man's land, housing, capital, and industry will continue to grow; the tens of thousands of yuan in dismissal fees for wives and concubines is merely a drop in the ocean compared to the total assets and is not something to worry about.

However, for men in the middle class and below, such a "wife" is difficult to cope with. Originally, it is not an easy thing for a person who "lives from hand to mouth," or who "cannot even get to the mouth from the hand," or even who "has a hand but no way to get to the mouth," to be able to marry a wife; some may have already spent a small capital. They cannot even maintain their own personal lives, and after marrying a wife, they have to support her like worshiping a bodhisattva. I ask, can the family economy not accelerate towards bankruptcy?

As the society becomes more and more depressed, a person without an economic backing has already been deprived of the qualification to marry a wife, but if he must take a risk, to taste the flavor of the fragrant, to avoid the butcher's door of the salted meat shop and gorge himself, then, I think it is best for him to vigorously pursue a working woman, to pursue a woman who can be diligent, thrifty, and hardworking, and who can engage in production. It is not necessary to insist on youth and beauty, nor is it necessary to ask whether she is a virgin or a widow. Of course, the kind of woman I am talking about does not necessarily refer to something like a "talented student from a certain girls' school." What I mean is that she must have at least a skill, and be able to support herself. But if she has received higher education, and at the same time can indeed provide her husband with strong help in terms of economy, then that is naturally the best. I have no name for such a wife, but I name her "economic wife," because she is as cheap and good as "economic vegetables."

However, one thing we must pay attention to is that the rights and obligations between wife and husband are equal. While the wife should help the husband materially, the husband should also strive to share the wife's labor and should not have the idea of ​​getting something for nothing and enjoying the fruits of others' labor. Because the wife is not a money tree after all, and the husband is not a capitalist, and cannot regard her as a wage laborer and exploit and squeeze her. Whether wife or husband should have such a understanding, that is: the family is like a small-scale cooperative, and she and he are shareholders in this society, and they should stand on the meaning of mutual assistance to produce and consume together.

The era of treating a wife with bound feet as a carved work of art has now passed. The views of praising love as sacred, being amazed by modern wives as heavenly gods, or regarding them as beautiful vases, these idealistic and aesthetic points of view are now also about to become inapplicable. In this era, wives have gradually become practical goods. On the one hand, society needs her to be an engine to promote social progress, and on the other hand, the husband also needs her to be his oil, salt, sauce, vinegar, rice, and society is the same to her husband.

However, coming back to the point. In the current situation in China, which is caught in the whirlpool of economic panic and where industry is backward, women's occupations are not developed, and the number of working women is extremely limited. Whether every man can marry a working woman as a wife, and whether every working woman is willing to marry a poor man, has indeed become a very big question. In addition, as the panic of unemployment deepens, even many men cannot find work to do, let alone women? Therefore, even if some people can marry working women as wives, whether the couple can often have work at hand is still a question. Taking a step back, even if they can have a relatively long-term occupation, whether the salary or wages they earn can solve their minimum living needs is still very difficult to say. In this way, "economic wives" are indeed not easy to obtain, even if you are lucky enough to obtain one, the result is probably still not very economical. As for the future, once there are little babies, the heavy burden on the family will naturally be expected. No matter how you control fertility, this group of "little troublemakers," this group of small "uninvited guests," may sometimes still intrude. This is like eating "economic vegetables," after paying for the food and drink, sometimes you have to pay a tip as well.

Therefore, if a man cannot afford to marry a wife, or if he is deeply afraid that marrying a wife will increase the burden of life and be unable to cope, then I still hope that he will violate his instincts and embrace celibacy. Otherwise, he can only use the methods I mentioned above as a last resort. Of course, if the wife of your dreams is a rich girl, that is naturally even better, but this depends on your environment and whether you have sufficient conditions to make her satisfied, otherwise you can't get her!

One last sentence: Although an "economic wife" may not necessarily live up to her name, a prostitute in a brothel is out of the question, because that is not only not very economical, but also a bit unhygienic; that is simply a multi-treasure wife!

"Too Old," "Too Young," "Just Right"—Three Laundry Women 262

— Bai Bi

This day was my first day working in the town. At breakfast, the office was changed to a dining hall. A head peered in from outside the dining hall, a middle-aged woman nearing forty.

"Sir, do you have any clothes to change today?" "No! No! No!" My colleague Old Zhang repeatedly spat out his disgusted reply.

"Sir! Let this old woman wash a few pieces, won't you? I may be old, but I still wash clothes clean. "She still wanted to salvage her fate.

"No!" Old Zhang was knocking on the table with his bamboo chopsticks. Disappointed, she glanced at me and rekindled her new hope.

"This newly arrived gentleman, do you have any?"

"No, I just changed them the day before yesterday," I replied honestly.

"Go away! Annoying! Muttering about what? Even if we have clothes, we wouldn't let you wash them." Old Zhang's face became a bit ugly.

After we ate our porridge, the middle-aged woman left. I was just about to ask Old Zhang, but he earnestly said to me first, "Old Yan, don't let that old woman wash your clothes from now on. There's a younger one here who washes well. She always comes here in the evening."

I gave him a smile. At night, the office turned into a night chat session.

Page 20

The door was closed, and the tall kerosene lamp cast an orange-yellow light. The documents on the desk had long been sleeping soundly in the drawer. At this moment, the table was filled with oranges, peanuts, and, of course, tea and cigarettes.

My colleagues were chatting about everything under the sun, and I recalled Old Zhang's words from the morning.

"In the first month, I think of my love, my love is like the New Year..." There was a faint female voice singing a spring tune, the sound waves coming from afar and approaching.

As it got closer, it seemed to be just outside the office door. "The flirt is here!" Old Zhang exclaimed with a humorous report.

Suddenly, the office door was pushed open, and a young woman of twenty-one or two appeared in the orange-yellow light.

"Gentlemen, have you had your supper?" Her eyes swept over the colleagues with a charming smile. "We've eaten," came the unanimous reply. After a brief greeting, she scurried off to the dormitory, rummaging through everyone's beds. Old Zhang followed closely behind.

"Ask for clothes properly, don't rummage around!"

"There's a secret in the quilt." Her voice was a bit oily.

"What secret?"

"Last night I dreamed of you..." "Bah! You bad seed, watch out for a slap." Her voice was a bit coquettish.

"XXXXXXXXXX"

"Don't get handsy."

When she came back out of the dormitory, she was carrying a large pile of clothes, at least six or seven sets. Four sets belonged to Old Zhang, and the rest belonged to two other colleagues. They were piled high on Old Zhang's desk.

Perhaps because there was a stranger like me present this evening, she didn't act too flirtatious in the office.

She sorted the clothes briefly, tucked them under her left arm, and said, "See you all tomorrow," then opened the door and left.

"In the first month, I think of my love, my love is like the New Year." Her voice bounced outside the door again.

Old Zhang seemed to remember something, and he also opened the door and went out.

That night, Old Zhang didn't come back.

○○○

Half a month later.

The middle-aged woman who usually came to mutter every morning at eight o'clock but always went back empty-handed suddenly disappeared. Instead, a young girl of about fourteen or fifteen came.

"You嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌My My My My My My My My My My My My My My My My

The little eyes also knew how to cast a good flirtatious glance. It hit Old Zhang, and she got a pair of his underpants.

When I saw her retreating figure, I quickly thought of a "flirt."

"Your mom is too old, you're too young." Old Zhang made another suggestive comment.

I couldn't help but worry about the young girl's precious youth.

Famous Quotes on President Chiang Kai-shek's "Working Principles" 263

— Yu

President Chiang Kai-shek recently drafted sixteen "Working Principles" to instruct his subordinates to follow. Among them, besides a few that are more suitable for military affairs, and without discussing them, now I will add my personal views and elaborate on the remaining principles as follows:

1. "Look at the big picture, start with the small details"—The success of any undertaking always comes from efforts in small details. Therefore, one should start with the small details when doing things. But while working on the small details, one must not overlook the big picture, so as not to have the disadvantage of caring for the small and losing the big. This is why one should look at the big picture and start with the small details.

2. "Don't lack a sense of responsibility when doing things"—A person's most valuable asset when doing things is a sense of responsibility. Without a sense of responsibility, it goes without saying that things will be started but not finished; even if they succeed by chance, it will always be a fluke. When Chinese people do things, they often don't know where their responsibility lies. This is true not only for public affairs but also for private matters. Therefore, this principle is truly one that everyone should follow.

3. "Knowing is difficult, doing is easy"—This saying was invented by Mr. Sun Yat-sen, and it contradicts the ancient saying that knowing is easy and doing is difficult. When we do things, we often know what should be done but not how to do it. This is clear evidence that knowing is difficult and doing is easy. Even if we don't know, we can still do it. We must adhere to this belief in everything we do.

4. "Say it and do it, finish it and then talk"—Consistency between words and deeds is also an important condition that must be followed when doing things. Many people can talk but not act, which is a big problem. Who can't talk big? But if you only talk without doing, then talking is as good as not talking. Therefore, you must put what you say into practice immediately. After you have finished what you said, then talk about something else.

5. "Be methodical and organized when doing things"—You must have a plan when doing things. With a plan, you can proceed step by step. Otherwise, you will be at a loss, unable to distinguish between urgent and important matters, and putting things in the wrong order, resulting in much effort for little result.

6. "Don't be perfunctory or shirk responsibility when doing things"—This is because you lack a sense of responsibility in everything you do, so you only want to be perfunctory in order to get rid of your responsibilities. When we do things, we shouldn't do them at all, but if we do, we must be responsible and see them through to the end. We must never be sloppy so that we can clarify where responsibility lies.

7. "When doing things, [only fulfill my responsibilities, don't shirk blame, and even more so, don't compete for credit"]—Most people like to compete for credit and shirk blame. When there is a mistake, they will try to shirk it in every way. Not only do they not regret their mistake, but they sometimes even implicate others. If they happen to achieve something, they boast and compete for credit. Little do they know that you must do your best, correct your mistakes, and not take credit for your accomplishments to be considered great.

8. "Look for things to do, don't wait for things to do"—Those who are willing to work should look for things to do; those who are unwilling to work can only wait for things to do. But those who wait for things to do often don't do their best when something comes up. Those who can truly do things must always look for things to do.

9. "Talk less, do more"—This is similar to the meaning of the fourth principle, which teaches people to work hard without saying empty words.

10. "Don't be ambitious or fickle when doing things"—This means that you should start with things that are easy to do, and you must have perseverance. If you are ambitious or fickle, you will rarely achieve anything.

11. "Be smart and concise when doing things"—You must be smart and concise in your work. But it is better to be slow and smart than to be concise and sloppy.

Mei Ying's Hands 264

— Ya Bin

Mei Ying is the maid at Mrs. Zhang's house, a beautiful, lively, intelligent, and lovely girl.

It is said that Mei Ying is only seventeen years old this year, but she has grown so tall; her good breasts are protruding, constantly undulating; her face is always red, like a newly opened peach blossom; her eyes are clear and watery, and when they move, it is like a drop of cool water rolling on a tender green lotus leaf, so bright and cheerful... In short, she is a healthy beauty, she has fully developed—However, what Mrs. Zhang is most satisfied with is her hands, her rich muscle so strong hands. Really, Mei Ying's hands, just like Mrs. Zhang's own something, as long as she is happy, whatever she wants, she simply says what is needed, Mei Ying's hands will give it to her. As for all the daily affairs of her home, such as cooking, sweeping, washing clothes, dressing the little Miss and the fourth young master,... she does not need to open her mouth, Mei Ying's hands always do it well for her.

There are many people in Mrs. Zhang's house! Mr. Zhang, Mr. Zhang's grandfather and grandmother, Miss Li Zhen, the eldest young master, the fourth young master (the second and third young masters are said to have died early), the little Miss, and Mr. Zhang's young mistress, together with Mrs. Zhang, there are a total of nine people. As for the maid, there is only Mei Ying. So all the daily affairs of this big family, even sending the little Miss and the fourth young master to school, fall on Mei Ying alone. If she was an ordinary person, she would not be able to cope with it. But fortunately, her hands are so useful. She gets up at six o'clock in the morning and starts sweeping the floor, turning on the water, cooking porridge, buying groceries, washing clothes, scrubbing the floor... All of these depend entirely on her hands. She is very good at using them flexibly, she can even do two things at the same time, such as cooking while washing clothes, knitting wool sweaters for the little Miss and the fourth young master, and also giving Mrs. Zhang chicken stew to nourish her stomach... This is impossible without her particularly flexible hands.

Therefore, Mrs. Zhang especially likes her, and even gives her five yuan a month in wages (it is said that maids in Shanghai mostly get three or four yuan a month), and sometimes even gives her some exceptions, such as letting her sell the monthly Shen Bao newspaper for money... etc. Mei Ying is of course very happy, and also works very faithfully for Mrs. Zhang, she never utters a complaint, always smiling. Whenever Mr. He, the tenant living in the pavilion room of Mrs. Zhang's house, asks her; "Mei Ying, are you very busy?" She always answers with a smile... "Nothing!" At the same time, those particularly strong hands are also constantly shaking, as if to indicate... They are very capable of listening to my use!

However, Dong Ping came. After several frosts and snows, Mei Ying's particularly strong hands became red and swollen day by day. Later, they even cracked and bled. But she seemed not to feel any pain, and was still happy to work. One day, Mr. He kindly said...

"Mei Ying, your hands!"

"Frozen, ah!"

"Buy some frostbite medicine and rub it on!"

"No, they will naturally get better next spring!"

She was still so happy.

But no matter what, Mei Ying's hands could not be used as flexibly as before. Washing vegetables, sweeping the floor, especially washing clothes, could not be done quickly either. So Mrs. Zhang's unhappy expression increased day by day, as long as she saw Mei Ying's hands, she would say hatefully... "Hum, hum, look at you' that ghostly appearance!"

One afternoon, it was snowing heavily, Mei Ying carrying a large water jug, went to the living room to ask Mrs. Zhang for two copper coins to make hot water to wash clothes. But somehow, Mrs. Zhang became stingy with two copper coins, she opened her fire-like eyes, and scolded Mei Ying...

"What must you make hot water? Isn't cold water good to wash with?"

"My hands are frozen, ah!"

"Frozen! How come they don't freeze when they're often outside? Sleeves are so short! Humph!"

"If the sleeves were longer, how could I do things!" But Mrs. Zhang seemed not to have heard, and said even more viciously...

"Often putting your hands outside, buying promiscuity! Thinking you're beautiful, seducing people!" Saying that, she rushed into her bedroom.

Mei Ying suddenly opened her eyes wide, as if she had lost her mind, standing there blankly without saying a word. After several minutes, she began to cry softly—this was her first cry!

But Mrs. Zhang said in the room... "Still crying! Not happy, are you? Get out of here next month!"

"Slee... sleeves... if they're... longer... can't do things, ah..." This was the only thing Mei Ying managed to say in her crying.

Responses to My Professional Introduction

The Soviet Russian Kerosene Industry 265

— Ye Huaming

The Soviet Russian kerosene industry has some shortcomings in the amount of kerosene production, oil refining and transport; between expanding the amount produced in new areas and its accelerating development; between expanding the amount of production and increasing the amount of natural oil refined. However, these difficulties, cannot stop the prosperity of the kerosene industry. The Soviet Russian kerosene industry is developing every day; and now it has already taken the second rank of the world kerosene industry.

The development of the Soviet Russian kerosene industry is very astounding, because in the previous Old Russia era the kerosene industry was very backward. The first World War, caused Baku—the greatest kerosene producing area of the Soviet Russian—to shrink its market. In the World War, the greatest blow to the kerosene industry was when the whole of the outer Caucasus was forcefully occupied by the troops of other countries.

At the end of the Great War, the Soviet Russian government was faced with an extremely difficult job. Most of the oil fields and kerosene wells were destroyed, and even those that weren't destroyed were mostly in a desolate state. This can be verified by the below facts... in 1913 when the Tsar was in power, the amount produced using the old methods was 9.13 million tons; but in 1920 to 1921, the total amount produced was only 3.78 million tons! In such a short period of time, what method should be used to cause the kerosene industry, to not only revert to the original state of 1913 but also greatly surpass it?

But after the Great War ended, the kerosene problem, was immediately taken with utmost importance, because the country was exactly needing oil to advance its industry and power stations.

With the common participation of all the workers of Soviet Russia, the kerosene industry began to rebuild anew. A large quantity of funding was assigned for the purpose of restoring the kerosene industry. In 1923 to 1928, a total of 628,000,000 rubles was spent. During the first five year plan, a total of 1,440,000 was spent.

Research on Current Affairs: The Problem of Raising Silver Prices 266

— Yimin

After Roosevelt came to power, in order to revive the American economy, in addition to implementing a controlled economy, monetary inflation, lowering the price of the US dollar, and buying gold, he recently put into effect the policy of raising the price of silver. After this news came, industrialists and businessmen, bankers, and all people in the government and the public concerned about the Chinese economy paid close attention. For a time, there were many discussions, so that the long-depressed silver problem became tense and important again.

The main purpose of the United States raising the price of silver is to develop trade in the Far East and compete with the British and Japanese forces. Because most parts of the Far East use silver, if the price of silver rises, it will be easier for American goods to be dumped in various parts of the Far East.

China is the main silver standard country in the Far East, and at the same time it is the largest country with an import surplus. If the price of silver is raised, it may seem to increase China's purchasing power on the surface, but in reality, it facilitates the dumping of American goods, completely taking away the domestic goods market that we are working hard to promote. Our national industry, under the devastation of imperialism, has long presented a crisis of bankruptcy; the reason why it can still linger on is that it still maintains a considerable portion of the sales market in the country. If this part of the domestic sales market is taken away by American goods due to the increase in the price of silver, then its future is truly unimaginable! At the same time, as the price of silver rises and American goods are dumped in China, the result will inevitably be a large outflow of our country's silver. According to the report of the Bank of China, the total amount of silver in Shanghai is... 142.48 million taels of silver, 33.678 million yuan of current silver, and 15,819 large bars. This is not a very large number either. If, under the dumping of American goods, our silver reserves decrease day by day as the number of import surpluses increases, it will make the economy unable to circulate, and even cause a great financial panic, leading to the disorder of the entire society—this can be foreseen.

But on the other hand, because the price of silver is raised, the trading of silver will inevitably become active, which is beneficial to general compradors and speculators. At the same time, if the price of silver rises and superficially increases our country's purchasing power, and practically facilitates the dumping of American goods, it will inevitably increase the revenue of our customs in the flow of silver in China. This is also conceivable.

These two phenomena that can occur as a result of raising the price of silver have defined the attitudes of our financiers, bankers, and industrialists towards this issue. Among them, some advocate postponing the approval of the London Silver Agreement and prohibiting the export of silver or levying export taxes on silver as a countermeasure against the United States' raising of the price of silver; others, on the contrary, say that the London Silver Agreement should be approved immediately to maintain international credit, and that prohibiting the export of silver or levying export taxes on it is a superficial view and that raising the price of silver is beneficial to us. As for who is right, in my opinion, it seems that they all have their reasons, but whether they are all speaking for the interests of the people and the masses is difficult to say.

How to Cater to the Psychology of Regular Customers 267

— Long Sheng

As the saying goes: "Everyone sells plaster, but each person boils it differently." This saying reveals the key to success or failure in all shop competitions. Often, in the same area, shops selling the same goods, why is it that one business has a constant stream of customers while the other is deserted? The reason is nothing more than one being good at catering to the psychology of customers, and the other not having grasped the knack of doing business. Therefore, you can determine the prosperity or decline of a business by observing the way shop assistants deal with customers. Based on my experience, I have written down a few common-sense points that shop assistants should have when dealing with customers, as a mirror for newly-fledged shop assistants.

(1) Show the Advantages of the Goods

I remember once going to a hardware store to buy a kitchen knife. The shop assistant took out several kinds of kitchen knives and displayed them for me to choose. At that time, I hesitated and couldn't figure out which knife was the best. Another shop assistant standing next to me noticed my hesitation and interjected, "Sir, please give me two copper coins." I searched in my pocket and gave him two copper coins. He stacked the two copper coins on the counter, picked up a kitchen knife, and chopped the two copper coins in half with a "swish" sound. So I bought this kind of knife that could chop copper coins without hesitation. This shows that it is easier to make people believe by practically demonstrating the quality of goods than by just saying empty words. For example, in a candy store, first give customers candy to taste; in a silk and satin store, unfold the cloth and drape it on the customer so that they can judge for themselves. These are all good ways to induce customers to buy with pleasure.

(2) Guide Customers to Buy

Suppose a customer originally only wants to buy a toothbrush. After the toothbrush is bought, the shop assistant can take out toothpaste and soap for the customer to appreciate. Often, things that could be not purchased for the time being, are desired to be bought unconsciously because the goods are pleasing to the eye, or are felt to be beautiful or cheap. Also, if the customer brings children, the shop assistant can take the opportunity to give the children things they like to play with. If there are items that make noise, it is okay to make them sound, so that the children cannot bear to let go. Parents usually love their children, and when they see things that their children like, they often buy them even if they didn't intend to.

(3) Know the Contents of the Goods

Now selling goods, if you don't know the contents yourself, then when you encounter experienced customers asking questions, you will be at a loss for words, wouldn't that be a joke? Therefore, shop assistants should first do some research on the contents of the goods they sell, such as the nature, manufacturing method, and place of origin of the goods. It is best to also understand the situation of similar goods, so that they can answer any questions customers may have with ease. For example, if a customer wants to buy a rosewood table, but thinks the price is too high, the shop assistant can first explain the advantages of rosewood, and then compare it with padauk, fragrant rosewood, etc. After hearing this, the customer will naturally know that rosewood is the best and will not think the price is too high and will be willing to buy it.

(4) Pay Attention to Attitude

When we go to stores opened by foreigners to buy goods, sometimes we leave without buying anything. When leaving, the shop assistants are mostly amiable and even express deep regret. However, the situation in stores opened by our own people is different. I have encountered many times that in stores, because the goods were not bought successfully, the shop assistants not only showed displeasure, but also ridiculed and scolded at will, making you embarrassed. This shows that the level of cultivation of Chinese and foreign merchants is obviously different. The following points should be constantly reflected upon by shop assistants to see if they have committed them. If they have, they should correct them thoroughly. (1) Asking customers how much the value of the goods they want to buy is: or asking customers whether they want to buy high-priced or low-priced goods, contains the meaning of despising customers. (2) Not immediately serving customers with shabby clothes. (3) Not answering customers' questions in detail. (4) Arbitrarily making fun of customers who have unusual physical features. (5) Clothes are not clean: fingers are dirty. (6) Whispering to each other, causing customers to suspect.

Travel Notes

Xia Men (Gorge Gate) 268

— Xiong Wan

", Xia Men has arrived!" The waiter shouted with a smile, raising his voice.

Passengers in the cabins and steerage all crowded towards the bow of the ship where the anchor was dropped. They opened their eyes wide. Their round, black eyeballs constantly scanned in all directions, surprised, seeming unable to find a target.

The mountains are still generation after generation, the water is still rushing.

"Where is Xia Men?" Someone in the crowd asked to himself.

The sharp bow of the ship broke through the waves, and sped forward, white waves surged up one after another, splashing the deck of the bow. The people in front retreated unconsciously, the wind howled loudly. "Xia Men?" There is still no shadow.

Woo woo! The whistle called frantically, the surging waves "he he" echoed, the wind became stronger, and also brought some small drops of water, falling coldly on the face. The noise gradually subsided, the situation seemed tight, everyone pressed their chests with their hands, trying to stop their hearts from pounding. The ship continued to move forward: still retreating one after another, but the waterway directly ahead seemed to be gone. Standing far ahead, head-on, was a majestic mountain, and the ship seemed to be heading straight for that mountain.

"Isn't that Baidi City? A waiter holding a kettle of boiling water" shouted loudly. Although the eyes of the crowd glanced briefly at a small red isolated temple on the mountainside, they hurriedly retracted and continued to look ahead: seeming to be thinking about the same question: "How will the ship go?" The water surface became narrower and narrower, the water flow became faster and faster, the mountains on both sides, like giants stretching their waists, were steeper than each other, and the bow of the ship gradually swung to the right.

"Ah!" Everyone suddenly seemed to understand and exclaimed. The waterway originally turned to the right along the mountain. The river became even narrower, really amazing, as straight as a small stream. Observing with the eyes, it seems that only one ship can pass. The mountains on both sides stand upright, like soldiers saluting, straightening their waists, and forming a vertical line with the water surface. Even if there is a small boat docked on the shore, no one can climb ashore. There is only yellow and black soil on the mountain: protruding boulders: things that look like dry branches. Although it is still summer, you can't find a clump of green grass. The wind howls frantically. People stand still like stones, as if they will only feel comfortable when they see the river surface suddenly widen. The light is too dim, if the clock in the living room didn't say that it was only a quarter past three, everyone would think it was dark. Really, even the blue sky is only left with a long strip hanging overhead.

. The mountains on both sides force the eyes to only look forward.

The waterway is always turning, and each turn gives people a hope and a disappointment. The word "ah" often flies out of people's mouths.

Another waiter with a kettle of boiling water came. He pulled a young man who looked like a student and said, "The first turning is Xia Men. Can you see it clearly? There are still more than seven hundred li to leave the gorge!" He looked at the waiter's face, and then looked at the mountain beside him that was only a few steps away, and slowly squeezed out a "um" from his mouth:

World Unemployment Figures in 1933 269

Survey Tang Qin

In 1933, the number of unemployed industrial workers worldwide was 45 million. The figures for the main countries are as follows:

United States 14,000,000

Germany 6,000,000

England 3,000,000

Italy 1,220,000

Japan 530,000

France 370,000

In addition to the 45 million to 50 million

unemployed workers worldwide, there are also quite a few unemployed farmers, small property owners, and intellectuals, floating in the raging waves of the world economic panic.

Our China is no exception. Just in Shanghai alone,

the panic in the silk, cotton, flour and other industrial sectors in recent years has caused 500,000 workers to become unemployed. In addition to these 500,000, there are also many semi-unemployed (reduced work and reduced wages, etc.) workers, as well as unemployed shop assistants, intellectuals, etc.

Humorous Anecdotes 270

— Shan Ben

One night, the philosopher Diogenes was walking in a big city. As he was crossing a street, he saw a soldier running towards him and asked: "Did you see a man running in front of me?"

"No"... why are you trying to hurt him? "He is a criminal."

"Criminal. What is a criminal?"

"A criminal is a man who engages in killing."

"Is that a butcher?"

"No. A criminal is a man who kills people."

"Okay, I understand. Is that a soldier?"

"Also no: a criminal is a man who kills people in peacetime."

"Then, is that an executioner?"

"Fool! A criminal is a man who kills people at home."

"Now, I understand very well: a criminal is a doctor."

Biography of a Famous Person Darwin (3) 271

— Ji Fan

Naturally, this kind of collection was regarded as the supreme comfort to him. When Stephen's famous "Explanation of British Insects" used the specimens collected by Darwin and titled: "Captured by Mr. Charles Darwin", he was really ecstatic. He felt as happy as a poet seeing his debut work printed. The person who had the most influence on Darwin during his time at Cambridge must be mentioned here. That is Professor Henslow. Mr. Heng was quite similar to Mr. Da. He lectured on botany and liked to use clear evidence, which was completely different from the lectures of other schools. He often took students to the field to practice collecting and explained rare plants or animals. Therefore, Mr. Da admired him very much at that time. The two of them became very good friends. Mr. Da often went to Mr. Ting's house for dinner, or the two of them took long walks. At that time, there was a saying in the school that Mr. Da "is the person who often walks with Mr. Henslow". Mr. Ting had a wealth of knowledge about botany, entomology, and was proficient in chemistry, mineralogy, and geology. He liked to start from small observations and observe the changes in the long-term continuation of observations, and then use them as conclusions. This research method later gave Mr. Da a lot of influence.

Mr. Da graduated from Huaiqiao University in 1831 and obtained a BA degree, which was the end of Mr. Da's school life. Undoubtedly, his academic achievements will be in his own efforts in the future: especially in the Beagle trip that will be specially mentioned below.

"What a glorious day November 4th is! My second life will begin from this day, this day will be considered like today's birth for all kinds of things in the future!" In October 1831, Darwin obtained the opportunity to travel on the Beagle, and he was appointed as the naturalist of the Beagle ship. The above words were what he wrote to Fitzroy, the owner of the Beagle ship.

Naturally, this trip was crucial for Darwin's academic achievements in the future. The tour of tropical countries that he had longed for in his childhood was now realized.

On December 27, the Beagle ship left England and began its world tour. The purpose of this voyage was to measure the coasts of "Chile" and "Peru" and the islands of the Pacific Ocean, and then continue the world tour to continue the exploration of the coastline. Therefore, we had to stay for some time in the places we passed. So, our naturalist, with the opportunity to go everywhere, either galloped on isolated islands, barren hills, or plunged into the thatched huts of barbarians, or swayed on small boats on the shores of the vast sea, or climbed the tropical forests on foot. He passed through the great desert, went to Fire Island, stayed on the top of the coral island, and he couldn't help but feel his own insignificance and the vastness of the universe in the vast tropical forest, and he couldn't help but feel nostalgic when he saw the naked body of the barbarian. During the trip, the main work was naturally to collect many kinds of animals and plants, make a rough dissection of them, and attach a simple narrative. Among them, the collection of crustaceans was the most complete.

This trip lasted for five years and two months. In the long journey, he trained him to work with concentration and focus: and aroused his interest in geology. Originally, he used to think that geology was boring, but now it has completely changed. "I have found a permanent and unremitting interest in geology, which has created a kind of"

Great ideas are also like astronomy to the universe. One thing, when he discovered the geology of Santiago, he was overjoyed. It can be seen that the interest in learning lies in practice, and only practice can grow people's research heart. Darwin was not used to hiring geological lectures, but his success came from travel and practical investigation.

This trip fully provided research data for the genius, expanded the genius's vision, and developed a difficult

determination, turning his life into a forward-moving stage.

So he had to smile at the "creation project" in the Bible, and at the same time he had to re-evaluate the value of the natural scientists of the past.

This trip is over, he published the famous "Diary and Notes". (To be continued)
